Industrial and Commercial Rehabilitation Association in Disaster Areas

Submitting a Petition to the Municipal Government to Exempt Donations and Taxes

The Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Rehabilitation Association in Disaster Areas yesterday submitted a petition to the Municipal Government, stating: "In order to petition for the exemption of donations and taxes in the disaster area, we respectfully request your review and approval to benefit the recovery of Jiangsu. On January 28th, the Japanese bandits caused disaster, and Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong and other places were the first to suffer a catastrophe. Industrial and commercial enterprises were either destroyed by the bombardment of artillery fire or looted by the Japanese bandits. The land is full of scars and scorched earth. It is not easy to recover, and the exemption of taxes and donations is the first priority. Although paying taxes is a national obligation that citizens should fulfill, it must also depend on the people's ability to pay taxes. If people are trying to survive, they don't even have time, and then they are taxed with various taxes and donations. It not only obstructs the future tax revenue of the country, but also drives the people into deeper waters. What's more, the disaster area in Zhabei, Jiangwan, and Wusong has suffered a catastrophe, and most of them have

sacrificed for the nation and the country. Our government should give special care and exempt all local taxes and donations, so that the survivors after the catastrophe will not have their livelihoods cut off due to the burden of heavy taxes, and industrial and commercial enterprises can gradually recover. The recovery of industrial and commercial enterprises is to cultivate the future tax revenue of the country, so the exemption of donations and taxes temporarily reduces its income in government finances, while the future national wealth is actually hidden in the dark. The so-called abandonment today, how can we not hope to be compensated in the future, and the grace to the disaster victims is also not small, which is beneficial to both the public and private. It is reasonable to submit a formal document, respectfully requesting your review and approval, and issuing a general order to comply with it, so as to benefit the recovery and show our willingness to help Jiangsu. It is most convenient for the public."

Songhu

Post-War Reconstruction Bonds in the War Zone Will Be Stopped

The 20 million yuan of post-war reconstruction bonds assumed to be issued at the second plenary meeting of the Post-War Reconstruction Committee in the Songhu War Zone will be stopped because of the government's financial difficulties and the difficulty in raising funds in the financial community. Only 800,000 yuan will be allocated by the government, and 300,000 yuan will be assumed by the local association, totaling 100

100,000 yuan, to serve as emergency relief funds for the war zone.

Opinions on Relief for Disaster Areas in Baoshan County

A Public Letter from Sun Xiwen

Sun Xiwen, the magistrate of Baoshan County, is quite enthusiastic about the relief of disaster areas in the county. He sent a public letter to the War Relief Association, stating his opinions. Now, the original letter is recorded below for your information:

"I have already reported to the provincial authorities about the devastation from the war in this county, as well as the findings from my inspections. I have also explained the situation in detail to Chairman Zhang, Mr. Jin Jushan, Mr. Hou Cheng, and others. When you were in the area, you showed deep concern for your hometown and felt the suffering deeply. I believe you have already been planning for the aftermath and relief measures. However, there are a few points that urgently need attention during implementation. Based on my limited understanding, I cannot remain silent and dare to offer my humble opinion for your consideration.

Baoshan County's agriculture, industry, and commerce have always been very weak. It is already difficult to make a living in normal times, so how can we withstand such a disaster again? Unfortunately, due to the recent events, the entire county has become a war zone. Considering the disaster situation in the three counties of Tai, Jia, and Bao, Baoshan County accounts for three-fifths of the total. Since the province has allocated funds for relief, the amount of funding should be determined based on the severity of the disaster. If the allocation is distributed equally by county, it will not be fair. It will be difficult to provide comprehensive relief to the more severely affected areas of Baoshan County. This is the first point that the Association should pay attention to regarding the allocation of provincial funds.

I have inspected the disaster areas extensively, and the impact on agriculture has been enormous. Small industries and businesses have also had their houses destroyed and their capital wiped out. The suffering of displacement and the difficulty of recovery are even greater than those of farmers. Most of the schools in the county have been occupied by the Japanese army, and there has been much damage, making it difficult to reopen them. Children have been out of school for too long, and they will become accustomed to idleness, which will become a burden on society. When implementing relief in the future, it seems appropriate to consider all of the above-mentioned sectors, distinguish between urgent and less urgent needs, and appropriately allocate funds based on the severity of the disaster. This is the second point that the Association should pay attention to regarding the allocation of relief funds.

This war has caused severe damage, and after last year's flood, agriculture, industry, and commerce have almost collapsed. If only relief funds are given without considering the aftermath, relief will never be thorough. When disaster victims receive relief, they may not have to worry about starvation, but after receiving relief, they will still be poor as before. The relief funds will be gone, and they will still be in urgent need of relief. The situation will be no different from before the relief. Generous assistance and helping the public are virtues cherished by Yao and Shun, but indiscriminate handouts are not favored by poverty alleviation policies in various countries. Therefore, this time, it is better to lend money at low interest rates than to give it away. If it is absolutely necessary to distribute emergency relief, it should be kept to a minimum. Giving provides temporary benefit; disaster victims see it as a windfall and spend it carelessly. Once it is used up, it is difficult to continue. If they have to repay a loan, they will inevitably work hard to manage their affairs. Even if they lose money, some of the principal will remain, which can be borrowed again. Livelihoods are difficult after a disaster, and many people will inevitably lose their jobs. If there is no plan to help them, it will cause social problems and burden public security.

In my opinion, if the funds allocated by the province are not large, in addition to emergency relief, four or five million yuan could be allocated to establish a lending office or a low-interest bureau, setting the lowest interest rate and a generous repayment period to provide working capital. If the funds allocated by the province are as expected, it seems that one hundred thousand yuan could be allocated to establish a local bank. On the one hand, low-interest loans could be given to agriculture, industry, and commerce to provide capital for operations. On the other hand, the county treasury could be managed to collect idle funds and use them to generate interest. This would not only regulate the local financial situation but also support various industries and provide them with opportunities for recovery. After the bank is established and the financial situation is fluid, further plans can be made. With the assistance of the local bank, efforts can be made to establish more small-scale factories, promote handicrafts, and accommodate the unemployed and vagrants, directly increasing production and indirectly maintaining public order.

The reason why Baoshan County's industry and commerce cannot flourish and local enterprises cannot develop is the lack of a financial institution to regulate them. Tai and Jia counties both have local banks, and their pawnshop businesses are particularly developed. Therefore, industry and commerce in these areas are generally more prosperous than in Baoshan County. Although they suffered the same disaster, local institutions were able to quickly establish a rough framework and carry out various tasks after the incident. This is partly due to the fact that these areas are wealthier and the disaster was less severe, but the main reason is the support of financial institutions. Finance is as important as the lifeblood of the human body. Post-disaster relief must consider long-term solutions. Baoshan County lacks financial resources and wealthy individuals, making it difficult to establish a bank even in normal times. After this devastating disaster, it is even more difficult to make it a reality. Although the funds allocated by the province are limited, they are the result of your efforts and appeals over the past few months, and it is not easy to obtain them. If the traditional relief methods can be changed and the distributed funds can be used as a fund for development, it will not only be consistent with the purpose of relief but also be a key to revitalizing the local economy. This is not only a win-win situation but also a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity. This is the third point that the Association should pay attention to regarding relief policy. I hope you will carefully consider and handle the above points. It would be a great blessing for the area."

Conclusion of the Taicang War Relief Association

Discussions on Reorganization Methods Yesterday

Since its establishment, the Taicang War Relief Association has devoted itself to registration, investigation, and the distribution of relief funds and grains. These tasks are now coming to an end. Therefore, yesterday afternoon at about 5 o'clock, a meeting of all committee members was held at the association's location at the bridgehead in Bentang Lane. At the meeting, everything was reported, and the reorganization of the Taicang branch of the Jiangsu Province War Relief Committee was discussed. Those present included Hu Cuishi, Hong Jingping, Huang Qiusheng, Huang Songsheng, Zhu Kaichuan, Zhou Kaisen, Zhu Qingzhao, Jin Xiawen, Huang Boxun, Qian Xingkui, and Ye Zhengong. Hong Jingping was elected as chairman, and Yu Tingwu was the recorder. After formalities, the chairman reported on all the past events. Then, the following proposals were discussed: (1) How to organize the reorganization of the Association into the Taicang Branch of the Jiangsu Province War Relief Committee. It was decided to have one chairman, two vice-chairmen, and six groups: General Affairs, Finance, Planning, Relief, Audit, and Statistics. Each group will have one director and one deputy director, as well as several staff members. (2) How to elect the chairman, vice-chairmen, and directors of each group. It was decided to elect Tang Weizhi as chairman, Xiang Huiqing and Gu Gongliang as vice-chairmen, Hong Jingping and Qian Xingkui as directors of General Affairs, Wang Boxun and Jiang Yuren and Wang Qihua as directors of Finance, Hu Cuishi and Lu Jingshi as directors of Planning, Jiang Hehang and Huang Songsheng as directors of Relief, Qian Songsan and Zhang Lunqing as directors of Audit, and Jin Xiawen and Zhu Qingzhao as directors of Statistics. Finally, Hong Jingping was elected to draft the association's constitution and rules of procedure. The meeting adjourned at around 7 o'clock.

Reorganization Plan of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company

Planning to Borrow Large Sums of Money

To Add New Shipping Routes

The Daily News reports that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, directly under the Ministry of Communications, has more than 30 branch offices along the Yangtze River and the coast. The total revenue is no less than tens of millions, but the expenses of the branch offices are too high, so the head office not only has no profit but also accumulates debts. Therefore, the Ministry reorganized the company on May 1 and appointed Chen Fumu, Vice Minister of the Ministry, as supervisor. After taking office, Chen immediately began to reorganize the company's affairs. The details are as follows:

Expanding Shipping Vessels and Repaying Old Debts

The Ministry of Communications believes that in recent years, China's doors have been opened wide, and foreign ships travel freely in the inland seas and rivers, causing domestic shipping companies to be excluded. At a time when the government is preparing to recover the shipping industry, it is necessary to actively expand domestic shipping in advance to meet future needs. The Ministry has ordered the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to draw up a sound plan to expand shipping vessels and to thoroughly repay the company's previous debts. It has borrowed 30 million yuan from the Dalae Company, of which 10 million yuan will be used to repay previous debts, and the remaining 20 million yuan will be used to purchase additional shipping vessels. It is reported that the loan has been negotiated and will be completed soon.

Scheduled Sailings on the Southeast Asian Route

The company already has domestic shipping routes, including Shanghai-Qingdao, Yangtze River, Shanghai-Guangdong, and Shanghai-Oujiang. It has not yet opened a Southeast Asian route, so Chinese expatriates doing business in Southeast Asia must travel on foreign ships. It is planned to open a Southeast Asian route to avoid the oppression of foreign ships. The company has purchased a ship from Norway and named it "Hai Rui" and "Hai Xiang" for exclusive use on the Southeast Asian route. It is reported that scheduled sailings will officially begin at the beginning of next month, exclusively for the use of Chinese expatriates doing business, in order to gradually recover China's lost overseas shipping rights. It is also understood that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has planned to reform the company's personnel and eliminate accumulated business malpractices.

A Record of the Xin Zhuang Military-Civilian Get-Together

Since the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, heavy troops have been stationed in Xin Zhuang Town, Shanghai. Zhao Junmai, the regimental commander of the First Regiment of the Customs Police Corps, is skilled in military administration and has strict discipline. The locals respect and love him very much. A military-civilian get-together was held at the Sixth Elementary School in the town the other day to demonstrate military-civilian cooperation and mutual assistance. The weather was clear and refreshing that day. The opening ceremony was held at 10 a.m. After formalities, Yang, the regimental adjutant, chaired the meeting and reported the purpose of the meeting. Zhang Zishi, a representative of the public group, gave a speech on the importance of cooperation and mutual assistance. This was followed by more than 30 entertainment performances. About 5,000 people attended the event, which was very lively. At the end, the local Maintenance Association presented a banner of political virtue, "Qin He Feng Gao," to express their appreciation.

More Than a Hundred Houses Collapsed in Dachang City

The Sound Was Like a Mountain Collapse, and the Scene Was Quite Tragic

Many Old People and Children Were Killed and Injured

Yesterday afternoon at 6 o'clock, the houses along the street at the eastern end of Hujia Muqiao in Dachang East Town suddenly collapsed. The sound was like a mountain collapse, and the cries of the old and young were very tragic. More than 100 houses collapsed in total. More than 20 residents of the houses were unable to escape. Several people have been rescued, but many more are feared to have been crushed to death. Some of the belongings and utensils in the houses had been moved out by the residents in advance, but those that were not moved out have been crushed. The houses in Dachang City are very old. During the Shanghai War, Japanese planes bombed and shells shook the ground, causing the foundations to crack. The large-scale collapse was indeed a tragic result of the war.

Ban on Using Straw as Wrapping for Imported Goods

The Commodity Inspection Bureau Notifies All Merchants to Pay Attention

Request to Correct Overcharged General Tax

Taxpayers' Association's Letter to the Public Works Department

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession received a letter from citizen Zhang Jianhou, stating that the Public Works Department was overcharging the general tax and requesting negotiation for a refund. Therefore, the association sent a letter to the Public Works Department to negotiate and immediately replied to Mr. Zhang. The Western letter is recorded below:

Letter to the Public Works Department: We are writing to you regarding the letter from Mr. Zhang Jianhou of No. 3, Lane 140, Xinzha Road, stating that the citizens have previously relied on your association to uphold justice in the case of the Public Works Department of the Public Concession overcharging the general tax, and that you have sent a letter to the bureau to stop it and replied to them, for which they are truly grateful. However, the bureau did not correct the overcharged amount and return it, but sent an English letter on May 7. At that time, the citizen was away on other duties and did not see the letter until he returned to Shanghai on the first of this month. The citizen does not understand English at all and was in the process of asking a friend to translate it. The other day, the Chinese tax collector of the bureau came to collect the summer general tax. The citizen explained the details in detail and asked him to correct it before taking it away. After a short while, two Westerners came again, their demeanor aggressive, and they threatened in broken Chinese that if the payment was not made, the door would be sealed immediately. We believe that the municipal general tax of the Public Concession is based on rent as the standard. Now, the Public Works Department arbitrarily increases it without seeking the facts, violating the established regulations. Moreover, the reasons stated are all one-sided opinions. According to their claim that due to the existence of a pavilion building, the rent should be increased by six yuan in foreign currency starting from January of this year, it has been found that the citizen moved in during the 14th year of the Republic of China, and the house already had a pavilion building, which was not newly built last year. The bureau has always collected taxes according to the rent and has never had any objections. This year, the people are suffering from the pain of violence and robbery, but they want to increase the burden, which is unreasonable and unjustifiable. It is also said that the citizen sublets the house to others, with an income of seventy yuan, and a net profit of fifteen to twenty yuan per month. This is even more absurd. Not to mention that the citizen does not have this income, even if he could sublet it for seventy yuan, how could there be a net profit of fifteen to twenty yuan, considering that the rent is fifty yuan, plus the city tax of seven yuan, as well as various expenses for electricity, certificates, telephone repairs, etc.? Isn't this just idle fantasy? The citizen is not repeatedly bothering your association for the sake of a mere ten yuan and eight cents per year, but for the sake of all the citizens, directly opposing the bureau's arbitrary increase in taxes and indirectly providing landlords with a basis for raising rents. Therefore, we dare to intrude and continue to request that your association uphold justice and forward a letter to the bureau to implement the correction. We will be deeply grateful for your public spirit, etc., and attach the bureau's letter to the association. We have found that the principle of finance should be simplicity and avoidance of harshness. Using the rent paid by the tenants as the standard for collecting municipal general tax is the most sufficient way to express simplicity and avoid harshness. Your bureau wants to increase taxes because of the subletting and the existence of a pavilion building. Then, in Shanghai, subletting is a common phenomenon. Should the municipal general tax be collected from the sub-tenants? And when the house is vacant and not sublet, can the general tax be reduced or exempted? As for building pavilion buildings, etc., it is even more evident that it is difficult for citizens to live and that rents are high. Furthermore, there are many houses equipped with water heaters, and their rents include the water heater rental fees. Logically, when collecting municipal taxes, the water heater rental fees should be deducted. However, your bureau mostly collects taxes including the water heater rental fees, and even the tap water fees included in the rent are also subject to the general tax. The same is true for the general tax of our association's office. In our association's view, fairness and non-disturbance are paramount in municipal administration. However, the bureau's approach is motivated by a desire to show fairness on the one hand and to increase public revenue on the other. However, it must be known that this is precisely the opportunity for lower-level officials to engage in "underhanded dealings," and as a result, the public revenue increases only slightly, while the losses suffered by the citizens are enormous. According to the aforementioned situation in the letter, we hereby request that your bureau carefully consider and return the overcharged amount. We earnestly hope for this. Addressed to the General Manager of the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department.

Reply to Zhang Jianhou: We are writing to you in response to your letter of June 9 regarding the Public Works Department's assessment of increased taxes, and the Public Works Department's letter has been carefully read. We greatly admire your attitude, as you neither give anything to others improperly nor take anything from others improperly, only following righteousness, which is the traditional spirit of our national culture. In addition to sending another letter to the Public Works Department to correct the matter, we are enclosing the Public Works Department's letter for your reference.

Request for Exemption of Land Tax and Water Fees in War Zones

(1) Letter to the General Manager of the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department: We are writing to you with the following request, and we earnestly hope that your association will consider and approve it. The Public Works Department of the Public Concession, in view of the people's suffering, has provided exemption from taxes. Real estate owners have also been exempted from rent based on the standards for exemption from the municipal general tax. We believe that during this period, water consumption must be extremely reduced, or even non-existent. If real estate owners have no income at all, and they still have to bear the responsibility of compensating for unused or used water fees, it would truly increase their losses. It seems inappropriate in terms of both law and human considerations. If your company can take into account the facts and exempt water fees in accordance with the Public Works Department's exemption measures, it would be greatly appreciated. We hereby request you to investigate and implement this.

Xue's Nephews Compete for Inheritance

First Instance Judgment Favors Nephews

Xue's Appeal Debate Also Concludes

After the wealthy merchant Xue Baorun died, leaving behind millions in inheritance, his sons Xue Gansheng, Yansheng, Jiasheng, Gensheng, etc., distributed it according to the will. However, his nephews Hua Yi and Hua Manyun came forward to claim their rights, citing the Kuomintang's party platform, the resolution on women's movement of the Second National Congress of the Kuomintang, and the current laws on women's inheritance rights, stating that although their mother Hua Xueqin had passed away long ago, they could legally inherit in her place. They requested that the defendants be jointly and severally liable to hand over all of Xue Baorun's inheritance, assign someone to liquidate it, and divide it equally. Since Hua and others were all minors, their father Hua Lihou, in his capacity as legal guardian, hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against the defendants in the First Special District Court. After repeated investigations by the court, the plaintiffs won the case, and the defendants were ordered to pay the two plaintiffs two-thirds of the total inheritance within 500,000 yuan. This is the first result of nephews demanding a share of inheritance from their uncles in an inheritance lawsuit in this city after the promulgation of the law on women's inheritance of property. Therefore, since the beginning of this case, lawsuits between nephews and uncles over the distribution of inheritance have sprung up. Although Xue lost the first instance, he was unwilling to yield. He hired lawyer Lin Yingqing to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, stating that the original judgment had not fully investigated the various points of law and fact claimed by the appellant, and he described them separately, divided into three parts: (1) The distinction between the beginning of inheritance and the right to inherit; (2) Regarding the second point of the original judgment, namely whether Xue Baorun's public inheritance had been divided; (3) The validity of the will. After the case was appealed, Hu Yigu, the presiding judge of the civil division of the Second Branch of the High Court, convened a collegial panel with two associate judges to hear the case. Most of the disputes were legal points, so the lawyers of both parties debated in great detail at the time, quoting extensively from scriptures and questioning each other, which took a long time. Presiding Judge Hu, for the sake of thoroughness, did not tire of deliberation and allowed both parties to fully express their views so that they could be selected. After they finished speaking, he announced the end of the debate and ordered both parties to leave, awaiting the scheduled pronouncement of the judgment.

Transportation Association Temporarily Suspends Passenger and Freight Transport

The Jinghu Railway Traffic Department resumed freight trains from the first of this month, tentatively scheduling one round-trip up and down freight train daily from Nanjing Riverbank to Maigen Road to meet urgent needs. Unexpectedly, due to the lack of locomotives, the freight cars that had been loaded since the second day have not been able to depart. The goods entrusted by customers to various transfer companies continue to arrive one after another, and the North Station has no warehouses to store them. Therefore, the Transportation Association convened a meeting the other day and decided to immediately notify all merchants that due to the lack of locomotives in the railway bureau, passenger and freight transportation will be temporarily suspended. They will notify them again once normal operations are restored.

Both Parties Have Sued in Court

Actors Tang Longquan, Zhang Guixuan, Lü Qifang, etc., performed at the Southern Theater opened by Wang Yushan in Nanyang Bridge, French Concession. At 10:00 PM on the first of this month, they settled their performance fees with the theater owner and the backstage manager Fan Yunqing, which led to a dispute. After Wang Yushan and Fan Yunqing, the plaintiffs, stated their complaints, the court briefly interrogated the defendants and then approved the postponement, pending the injured person's recovery before further interrogation.

Shareholder of Hesheng Bank Accuses Manager

Using Hesheng's Capital

For Speculative Transactions

Chuan Zidong from Sichuan recently hired a lawyer to file a criminal private prosecution with the First Special District Court, accusing Shen Shihua of breach of trust. The gist of his complaint is that in September of last year, the defendant Ao Min and other shareholders raised 30,000 taels in ten shares, each share being 3,000 taels, and opened the Hesheng Bank in Fuxing Lane, Beijing Road. Min recognized one share, and the contract stipulated that the business would be operating securities and earning interest. At that time, the defendant was elected as the manager. It was found that there were three ways to operate securities: (1) receiving interest on time; (2) entering and exiting at any time; (3) earning interest through arbitrage. Unexpectedly, the defendant violated the agreement and used Hesheng's capital for speculative trading, damaging the shareholders' property, which constitutes the crime of breach of trust under Article 366 of the Criminal Law. Moreover, according to the contract, Hesheng's scope of business was limited to shareholders, but the defendant also bought and sold public bonds on behalf of customers, which also constitutes breach of trust. Therefore, he filed the lawsuit. The afternoon before yesterday, Judge Feng of the Special Court opened a court session for questioning. The defendant failed to appear. The plaintiff's lawyer stated the case, and Judge Feng ordered the case to be postponed and summoned the defendant to appear for further questioning.

China-Germany Trading Company Seeks Domestic Product Samples

Niu Zhipeng and others, the founders of the Northwest China-Germany Trading Company, have been serving in military, political, and transportation agencies in Shaanxi for many years and are very familiar with the situation in the Northwest. They deeply lament that foreign goods are flooding the markets everywhere, resulting in huge losses, while domestic goods have disappeared from the Northwest, which is extremely painful. Therefore, in November of last year, they organized the Northwest China-Germany Trading Company, with the English name (WorldtradingCo), to develop the Northwest, promote domestic goods, transport well-known local products from various regions, and develop commerce to alleviate people's livelihoods. Unfortunately, the Japanese army invaded Shanghai, and war broke out suddenly, causing obstacles and great losses. After the end of the Shanghai War, they immediately went to Shaanxi to replan, established a head office in Xi'an, and planned to establish branch offices in Shanghai and Lanzhou. Mr. Niu came to Shanghai on the 11th (residing at No. 5, Laolaoxiudeli, Baik Road) and is collecting domestic product samples. He sincerely hopes that domestic product factories in this city will send a copy of their samples and agency regulations for selection and negotiation.

Central Bank Inspection Report

127th Time

Central Bank's 127th Issuance Preparation Inspection Report: According to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the issuance of exchangeable notes by this bank. The 127th inspection was conducted on June 10, 21st year of the Republic of China, by Supervisor Wang Yihou at the bank's issuance bureau. The inspection results are announced as follows: (A) Total amount of exchangeable notes issued: 29,399,340 silver dollars, including 26,670,525 silver dollar notes and 2,728,815 subsidiary coin notes. Total amount of exchangeable note reserve funds: 29,399,340 silver dollars, including cash reserve of 23,875,906 silver dollars. This cash reserve includes 21,294,790.81 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuance vault, 1,428,893 silver dollars stored in branch offices in various ports, and 1,152,222.19 silver dollars stored with other banks. The security reserve is equivalent to 5,523,434 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of customs gold exchangeable notes issued: 375,000 customs gold units. Total amount of customs gold exchangeable note reserve funds: 375,000 customs gold units. This reserve fund includes 150,000 US dollars, stored with banks in this city, at a fixed price of 40 customs gold units as above. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Exchangeable Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the security reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the security is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. June 10, 21st year of the Republic of China, Central Bank Supervisory Committee.

Education News

Important News

Mayor of Peiping Advocates

Peaceful Resolution of Student Protests

Two Demands of the Normal University Accepted

Students from China College on Strike in Support

Peiping, 11th – As of 9 PM tonight, police and students are still in a standoff in front of the Normal University. The Student Union issued a general strike declaration, opposing Shen Yinmo and the fascistization of education in China. Injured police have been sent to the hospital. Students claim that three students, one cook, and one school worker were arrested. The Normal University School Protection Committee presented four preconditions for negotiation tonight: (1) Withdraw the military and police; (2) Restore telephone service; (3) Release arrested classmates; (4) Written apology. The content of the negotiation concerns ensuring the safety of vehicles leaving southwards, and compensation for losses, all to be borne by the municipal government, with a full response required before 9:30 PM. Peiping Mayor Zhou Da-wen stated that he advocates resolving the student protests peacefully and has telegraphed Zhu Jiahua, asking him to find a solution as soon as possible to prevent the student protests from escalating. Regarding the four conditions raised by the students, he believes it is best not to raise conditions and to handle the matter through legal procedures. The first two conditions have already been implemented. As for the third, the arrested individuals will be released if the students do not proceed to the train station. Regarding the fourth, since the military and police were also injured, an apology should be considered at length. After 9:30 PM tonight, over three hundred batons from the Boy Scouts of the Normal University Affiliated High School were transported to the Normal University, and the number of patrol police was also increased, making the situation more serious. China College has now gone on strike to support Normal University and other colleges.

Peiping, 11th – The preconditions for negotiation between Normal University and the authorities have not been established as of midnight. Normal University students have formed ten volunteer night patrol teams, patrolling the school. Police, security forces, and fire brigades are on high alert outside the school. Telephone communications for all colleges and universities have been cut off.

Su Provincial Education Director Zhou Fo-hai

Letter to Colleagues in the Education System of Jiangsu Province

(I)

A letter from Zhou Fo-hai, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, to colleagues in the education system of Jiangsu Province: I have been appointed to head the education system in this province for several months now. I have long known that Jiangsu's culture is the best in the southeast, and its education system is a model for the whole country. I believe that my abilities are limited, and I deeply fear that I will not be able to meet the expectations of the people of Jiangsu. Furthermore, with the treasury empty and the national crisis not yet over, the difficulty of the situation is beyond what I initially expected. Therefore, since taking office, although I have worked diligently day and night and made every effort to plan, I have ultimately been unable to make any significant achievements. However, I am confident that I have always been impartial in dealing with matters and sincere in treating people. Therefore, in the midst of difficulties and challenges, I have received the benefit of assistance and support from gentlemen in the education sector, and I have fortunately avoided criticism for failure. This is something that I am deeply grateful for and will continue to strive for. However, I have silently observed that the education system in Jiangsu has been showing signs of fatigue and decline in recent years. If we do not seek to revitalize it at this time, I fear that there will be no way to salvage it in the future. Therefore, I believe that the education system cannot be controlled by the efforts of one or two officials. Administrative organs occupy a guiding and promoting position, while those who are responsible for molding and shaping character are still the teachers and staff who directly provide education. Only when the two can connect with sincerity, regulate each other with righteousness, and be closely linked, like the response of fingers and arms, can the effectiveness of education be expected. The teachers and staff in Jiangsu are all honest and understanding individuals, and they are already clearly aware of the principles. There is no need for me to repeatedly explain them. However, I usually lack opportunities to contact you all, and I do not want there to be any distance in our intentions. Therefore, I have chosen one or two observations that I have made and offer my humble opinions in the hope of discussing them with you all. (To be continued)

World Games

Puppet State Participating

丨Shen Siliang's Sighs丨

Will Telegraph the Committee to Inquire About the Truth

If It Is True, Will Strongly Oppose

Japanese Intrigues Will Involve Many Twists and Turns

Sports and Diplomacy?

It was reported yesterday that the puppet state of Manchukuo, through the negotiations of the Japanese delegation, will be allowed to send two athletes to participate in the World Games this autumn. After this shocking news spread, everyone expressed opposition. This reporter specifically visited Shen Siliang, honorary secretary of the National Sports Federation, to obtain his opinion, as follows:

Cannot Use India and the Philippines as Examples - The participation of "Manchukuo" is based on the precedent of India and the Philippines. However, India and the Philippines are dependent countries, but "Manchukuo" is neither a dependent country nor an internationally recognized independent country. What precedent does this follow?

Will Telegraph to Inquire About the Truth - This news has not yet been officially announced by the committee. Since there is this claim, the federation will immediately telegraph the committee to inquire about the truth. If it is true, it will strongly express its opposition to the executive committee of the committee.

Japanese Tricks - The puppet state's request was made by the Japanese on its behalf. The situation is clear at a glance. It is naturally a trick played by the Japanese. There will be many twists and turns in the future. Strong opposition and protests may have little effect. His sighs showed his profound concern.

Cannot Help But Sigh at the Olympics

Germany's Hopes Are Slim

Economic Decline Affects Sports

Talent Is Buried, Performance Declines

丨Our Country Is Even Worse Than Them丨

Germany occupies a strong position in the world of sports. This World Games should be full of hope. Unfortunately, the tide of the world economic decline is hitting Germany, and it is at the center of it. Hopes will be greatly affected. It is reported that only nineteen male and female athletes will be sent, and their performance has greatly declined. One can only sigh in frustration.

The Plight of the Sports World - Economic decline has recently created obstacles for sports in Germany. The fear of unemployment has made the number of spectators in European competitions shockingly low. Hopeful athletes in various sports associations are therefore unable to train to the standards of world competitions. Training requires competitions. With fewer spectators, major sports events become wait-and-see affairs. Germans are not as enthusiastic about track and field as they are about boxing and soccer. A sports event requires at least six world-class athletes to attract an audience, and hiring world-renowned performers is not economically feasible.

Hopes Are Weakened - Athletes lack opportunities to test their performance and gain experience in international competitions. This is why hopes for the Olympics this autumn are weak. Although there are many talented young students, there have been good performances in junior sports events, but these can only be considered future hopes. The German Minister of the Interior once tried to reorganize the national sports organizations to seek progress, but the result was abandoned due to economic problems.

A Glimpse of Declining Performance - Thus, the discovery of talent can only be obtained by chance. Progress is therefore difficult. Last autumn, the German National Championships were held in Berlin and Magdeburg. The German press unanimously expressed disappointment, with no records broken. Twenty-Four

Mr. Zhu went inside, drank a cup of tea, and then said, "Zhong'er! Please take me to see where the school should be set up." I led Mr. Zhu to see the main hall, where the Tathagata Buddha is enshrined. Then we looked at the back hall, and Mr. Zhu suddenly asked, "How come there's a Taishang Laojun in a Buddhist temple? Strange! How did Buddhism and Taoism compromise?" I told him, "The monks added him five years ago because the donations weren't enough to cover expenses. Originally, there was a Zixia Cave about ten miles away from here. All the villagers who believe in Taoism go there to burn incense. When we consecrated the Taishang Laojun here, the monks said triumphantly, 'This profit will no longer leak out.' Indeed, since the Taishang Laojun came, the temple has earned an additional fifty or sixty yuan each year. These monks really know how to do business."... We walked, and soon we arrived at another hall. Mr. Zhu asked, "What are these Bodhisattvas? I recognize the God of Wealth! What are those?" I answered one by one, "This is the Smallpox God, this is the Silkworm God, this is the Ox God." Mr. Zhu said, "I guess all of these are probably employees of the monk boss, right? Which one is the best at doing business?" I said, "That depends on the year. The year before last, there were the most children with smallpox, and the Smallpox God was in luck. Last year, the spring silkworms had a plague, and the Silkworm God's business was even better than the God of Wealth." Mr. Zhu said, "What an interesting shop this is!" I said, "Now that we're going to turn it into a school, we have to move these Bodhisattvas around so that the elementary school students have a place to sit. Elementary school students are our living Bodhisattvas. When they all sit here, the temple will definitely have a new look." Mr. Zhu began to say things that I couldn't understand. He sighed and said, "If you call the elementary school students to sit here one by one, they will also become clay and wood sculptures of Bodhisattvas. Then these children will become the teacher's little helpers, just like the Bodhisattvas doing business for the monks. Won't there be too many Bodhisattvas and too many elementary school students? What kind of medicine is in this gourd?" Mr. Zhu continued to ask, "Is there anywhere else to see?" "No!" was my short reply. Mr. Zhu said again, "A school is like an old ox, and these few rooms are just a hair on the ox's body, just a hair!" I was very anxious in my heart. Mr. Zhu obviously looked down on our ancient temple. I was extremely worried that he wouldn't want to be our teacher here. What, what, what should I do?

Ministry of Education Prepares for National Sports Conference

Publishes Ten Articles of the Organizational Outline of the Preparatory Committee

And Sets the Preparatory Meeting for the 16th of This Month

After the Ministry of Education submitted the organizational outline of the National Sports Conference Preparatory Committee to Mr. Chu Minyi, it sent Li Zheng, Director of the Department of Social Education, to discuss the matter with Mr. Chu. It was decided that the Ministry of Education would convene the first National Sports Conference in Beijing in mid-August this year. The organizational outline of the Preparatory Committee was submitted by the Ministry of Education to the Executive Yuan meeting and was approved on the 10th. It was also stipulated that the estimated budget would be 12,700 yuan. The Ministry of Education then, on the 11th, followed Article 2 of the organizational outline of the Preparatory Committee and hired Chu Minyi, Zhou Yawei, Wu Yunrui, Huang Mingdao, Zhang Zhijiang, and other five people as hired preparatory committee members, and hired Mr. Chu as the director of the Preparatory Committee. It also designated Guo Xinsong, Director of the Department of Higher Education of the Ministry of Education, Gu Shusen, Director of the Department of General Education, Li Zheng, Director of the Department of Social Education, and Peng Baichuan, Section Chief, as ex officio members. It was decided to hold the first preparatory meeting at the Ministry of Education on the 16th of this month to discuss the preparatory steps and determine the date of the conference. It is also heard that the convocation of this National Sports Conference and its rapid preparation are due to Mr. Chu Minyi's strong support, so there should be no difficulties with funding and other matters.

Organizational Outline of the National Sports Conference Preparatory Committee of the Ministry of Education

Article 1 This committee is designated as the National Sports Conference Preparatory Committee of the Ministry of Education, organized by the Ministry of Education.

Article 2 The number of members of this committee shall be five to nine. In addition to the directors and section chiefs of the competent departments designated by the Ministry of Education as ex officio members, experts in domestic sports or people who are enthusiastic about promoting sports shall be hired.

Article 3 This committee shall handle all preparatory matters for the National Sports Conference, starting from June of the 21st year of the Republic of China and ending on the day the conference concludes.

Article 4 The office of this committee shall be located in the Ministry of Education in Nanjing.

Article 5 This committee shall have a director who shall manage all preparatory matters.

The director shall be hired by the Minister of Education from among the members of this committee.

Article 6 This committee shall have a documentation, editing, affairs, and reception group, each with a group head, who shall be hired by the director from among the members of the committee, and shall have several group members who shall be responsible for the affairs of the group, who shall be hired by the director.

Article 7 In addition to the members of this committee being assigned to various affairs, staff members of the Ministry of Education may be assigned to serve concurrently, and temporary staff may be hired.

Article 8 The positions of the staff of this committee are all honorary positions. Except for office expenses that may be paid for official business, no salaries shall be paid, but this shall not apply to temporary employees.

Article 9 This committee may hold committee meetings and group meetings. The dates shall be determined by the director or group head at any time.

Article 10 This outline shall be approved and implemented by the Minister of Education.

Free Talk

Ma Xiangbo, a 93-Year-Old Man, Records

The Way to Preserve Health

— Plum Blossom

The way to preserve health, in a nutshell, is to not destroy one's nature. The destruction of nature begins with the extravagant use of spirit. Spirit needs to be used, but if it is wasted, it will hurt one's vitality.

Eating, dressing, prostitution, and gambling are all manifestations of the extravagant use of spirit. The rushing about, scheming, stirring up trouble, and making waves of bureaucrats and politicians are also nothing more than the extravagant use of spirit. If you want to ask me how to preserve health, I can't say anything profound other than preserving my nature. Hygiene is certainly important, but hygiene is not necessarily able to prolong life.

Confucius was the most particular about hygiene. Confucius was the most particular about diet. He had the strictest dietary conditions. "Food that is spoiled and stale, fish that is rotten, and meat that is spoiled, he does not eat. Food that is discolored, he does not eat. Food that smells bad, he does not eat. Food that is not properly cooked, he does not eat. Food that is not in season, he does not eat." Even "If the meat is not cut properly, he does not eat. If he does not get the right sauce, he does not eat." Confucius was so particular about his diet, but he only lived to be seventy-three years old.

My father lived to be seventy-five, my mother lived to be eighty-nine, and my sister lived to be ninety-three. They were not very particular about their diet, but they all had one unified good habit, which was getting up early. They all had the spirit of the ancients of "rising at the crowing of the rooster."

I have had the habit of getting up early since I was a child. My mother would tell me to recite scriptures and memorize books in the early morning. Sometimes, I would get out of bed and start mumbling scriptures before I even had time to get dressed.

Most people in Shanghai do not have the habit of getting up early, but they used to be very good at getting up early. When I first came to Shanghai, shops had to remove the door panels and open their doors after sunrise, otherwise idlers would come to knock on the door and shout:

I think that now, if you open your shop door at sunrise, people will definitely laugh at you for being crazy.

Harbin

— Feng Ji

Since the brutal Japanese occupation of the Three Eastern Provinces, Harbin has become a arena of contention for Japan and Russia. China adheres to a policy of non-resistance, and to this day remains at a loss. However, the righteous army, with surging hot blood, gallops across the land, displaying a spirit of vowing to recover our territory. The importance of Harbin's position is evident. Recounting its recent brief history may be what readers wish to see.

Harbin is a Manchu word. During the Qing Dynasty, it was governed by the Deputy Lieutenant-General of Acheng. Thirty years ago, it was desolate and lonely, merely a village of three to five fishing families.

In the twenty-second year of the Guangxu reign, the Russians demanded that it be opened as a commercial port. For the sake of fostering friendly relations, our country agreed to designate five hundred square li as a Russian concession. The name of Harbin thus became prominent. In less than twenty-five years, it transformed into an important commercial center in East Asia, comparable to Tianjin in the north and Shanghai in the south. The Russians even called it the "St. Petersburg of the East," and some even presumptuously called it Tokyo, regarding the Russian St. Petersburg as the Western capital.

Harbin is located in the center of Manchuria and Mongolia, serving as the key to North Manchuria. Its transportation is convenient, with waterways including the Songhua and Heilong Rivers. Upstream, it sails to Fuyu, Laoshaogou, and other ports; downstream, it passes through Yilan, Fujin, Heihe, and other places, directly reaching the Russian territory of Boli and Miao'erk. By land, it connects to Changchun in the south, linking with the South Manchurian Railway, reaching Japan and Korea. To the east, it reaches Vladivostok; to the north, it connects with the Ussuri Railway, directly reaching Europe via Siberia. With connections in all directions, it is truly an important town in the Far East and a key port in North Manchuria.

The important areas of Harbin are the Daoli and Daowai districts. Daoli was originally called Bazhan, and Daowai was originally called Butou. Because they are separated by the railway, they are referred to as "inner" and "outer." Daowai is entirely a Chinese commercial area, with almost no Russians residing there. Daoli, on the other hand, is purely a Russian commercial district, with some Chinese residents as well. The commercial conditions in the two districts are vastly different, and the municipal management is consequently divided into different levels. However, since the European War, the Russians have been unable to build, and the market is inevitably desolate. There are many hotels, and they are all very clean. Transportation includes automobiles, horse-drawn carriages, and rickshaws. Horse-drawn carriages cost seven or eight jiao per hour, while rickshaws are slightly cheaper. The drivers in Daoli are mostly Russians, with some Chinese as well. If one does not know Russian, it is quite difficult to hire a carriage.

The most bustling street in Daoli is Zhongguo Dajie (Chinese Street), where everything is available. The railway station is not far from Yaopu Jie (Pharmacy Street) in Daoli, and it takes twenty minutes by horse-drawn carriage. There are joint tickets to Beiping, Hankou, Shanghai, Vladivostok, Korea, and Japan. However, to purchase these joint tickets and sleeper tickets, one must pre-order them at the International Bus Ticket Office diagonally opposite the station. These types of joint tickets are not sold at the station.

On the Seventh Day After Lesser Fullness of Grain in the Ren Shen Year, Accompanying Xuan Ge to Visit the Tomb of Zhu Guwei Zongbo on Holland Road

— He Chai

The early summer is clear and peaceful, the rain has just cleared. Holland Road is remote, willing to travel together. Still watching the peonies unfold their golden belts, and witnessing the Hibiscus put down its arms. Luxuriant is the fine city, the lyricist is gone. Loud and clear is the old history, the remonstrance rings. (In the Gengzi year, the Duke was a lecturer in the Hanlin Academy, submitting a memorial strongly requesting the suppression of the Boxer bandits.) There is no need to speak of the changes and vanishings of floating clouds. Only wishing to offer a cup during flowering time.

Tang Duo Ling

— Xuan Ge

In early summer, accompanying Master He Chai to visit the tomb of Zhu Guwei Zongbo, the soft rain has cleared. The breeze is gentle, the fan is not needed. Quietly, the new green splashes across the suburbs. Passing the late spring is all resentment. Do not forget. It is in the mountain spring. Who recognizes the old frost string? The literary ancestor sleeps underground. Writing autumn lyrics, bleak and desolate Youyan. Heartbroken, the cormorant soars across the sky. The affairs of this world. Are too soaked in suffering.

One Laughable and Pitiable Incident

— Gong Yu

Recently, a friend came from another port and told me of an incident that can serve as a valuable lesson for travelers. My friend said, "This time, I came to Shanghai by train. When boarding, the passengers were not very crowded. There was a young woman with a beautiful appearance and particularly luxurious and fashionable attire. She boarded at the same time as me, and our seats were also close. There were few passengers in the car, and even fewer women. The young, fashionable woman was the only beautiful one, so the passengers all stared at her, making her the center of attention. However, she remained calm and composed, showing no shyness at all. She must have received a school education or be what is called a modern girl. Soon after, the train arrived at a station, and several passengers boarded, filling the empty seats. Before long, it arrived at a major station, and even more passengers boarded and disembarked. The car immediately felt crowded. A young man in a Western suit, carrying a leather bag, boarded the train and looked around, seeing that there were no empty seats. He showed a slight look of displeasure, but then he was delighted and went straight to the woman. She was taking up a lot of space, and others may have thought that she was a young, fashionable woman and felt ashamed of their own appearance, not wanting to squeeze next to her, so they let her be. This young man's psychology was completely opposite, and he took pleasure in sitting next to a beautiful woman, so he went straight to squeeze for a seat. At first, the woman felt very comfortable taking up more than one seat, but when the young man sat down, she felt it was too narrow, as if they were a related pair. After several more stops, passengers got on and off at each stop. Few people who had originally seen the woman board alone remained. Those who boarded later saw the woman and the young man sitting side by side, and many mistakenly thought they were a loving couple or lovers. However, I never changed my seat and watched coldly from the sidelines, knowing everything clearly. Suddenly, I heard the two of them chatting intimately, and I was very surprised. I secretly thought that the so-called social openness of modern times, which eliminates the boundaries between men and women, was indeed like this. Then, the train arrived at another station and stopped abruptly. Of course, passengers got on and off. The woman stood up and leaned against the window, watching the scenery outside. The young man also stood up, placing one hand on her shoulder, acting even more like a married couple. Suddenly, the woman exclaimed, "Oh no! What should I do?" The young man quickly asked what was wrong. The woman said that the diamond hairpin inserted in her hair had suddenly fallen outside the train. There were many pedestrians, and it would soon be picked up by someone else. What to do? What to do? The young man leaned out the window and looked. Indeed, it was there. So he bravely said, "You stay here and watch it. Let me get off the train to pick it up." With that, he hurriedly"

On Thrifty Frugality to Save the Nation (9)

— Narrated by Nie Zengjifen, Written by Son Qijie

The situation at that time was very similar to today. The lamentations of Guan and Meng, and the weeping of Cao Sheng, all stemmed from this. Gathering a large number of people who value profit over righteousness and lack integrity, even if you save them with ten times the military equipment of Europe and America, they will only harm themselves and provide resources to the enemy. On the contrary, if you can practice the teachings of etiquette, righteousness, integrity, and shame, then acts of greed, evil, filth, and inferiority will not be tolerated by public opinion, which is more powerful than the punishment of the law. The habit of extravagance and deceit will be abandoned by society, and its effects will be more effective than the restrictions of political decrees. In this way, people will have a barrier in their hearts for defense and protection. Merchants will not covet foreign goods and sell them for profit, and citizens will not covet the exquisite and convenient imported goods and buy them. This is truly a method of strengthening the walls and clearing the fields. Today, the financial panic in various countries shows signs of imminent collapse. Countries that rely on military force to dominate and economic aggression are likely to collapse sooner or later. Those that temporarily avoid collapse do so by using the resources and wealth seized from the countries they have invaded. For example, our country spends a huge amount of 200,000 million yuan each year on foreign goods, at least half of which is used to supply the enemy's army, navy, and air force, as well as materials for bombs and weapons. Everyone is unwilling to bear the infamous name of providing money to the enemy, but this is actually happening, driven by desires. These are the Han traitors and national sellouts in our hearts. If everyone can remove the thieves in their hearts, then all the enemy's instruments of aggression will be useless. At that time, people in all countries will also realize the goodness of this method and quickly imitate it, removing their extravagant habits, abolishing their useless industries, and reducing their suicidal military preparations. They will return to simplicity and foster good neighborly relations. World peace can be achieved easily, and the key lies in each individual's self-discipline and control of desires. If desires do not stop for a day, then the enemy's source of supplies will not be exhausted for a day, and the war will not stop for a day. The impact of individual desires on world order and chaos is so great.

After the young man picked it up, he hurriedly got back on the train, revealing a smug look. However, after getting on the train, his expression suddenly changed to one of panic, looking around as if he couldn't find a seat when he first boarded the train. I was puzzled at first, but then I realized that the woman was gone. Only then did I understand the young man's panic. The young man searched up and down in his original seat for a long time, his face becoming increasingly pale and dejected. A neighbor asked him what was wrong. The young man said, "I lost a leather bag, which contained important documents and 3,000 yuan in cash. The value of the documents is ten times that of the cash. Have any of you seen it?" The neighbor said, "Why are you so panicked? This leather bag is still in the hands of your family member and went off the train with you. Why did you get back on the train alone?" The young man didn't understand at first, but then he realized and couldn't help stomping his feet and saying, "I made a mistake! I made a mistake! She's not my family member and I've never met her before. I only met her on the train." The neighbor still didn't understand, but I understood everything clearly and found the young man both laughable and pitiable."

Eating Meat Is Not As Good As Eating Fish

— Shou Zhen

Scientists have studied various meats and their nutritional value, and have determined that fish is quite high in value. Fish can provide the vitamins and minerals needed for a healthy life. Fish contains oil, minerals, and protein in no less quantity than meat.

Fish are particularly rich in minerals: magnesium, sodium, potassium, iodine, mineral yellow, green gas, etc. Fish oil, especially cod liver oil, is rich in vitamins A and B. Fish roe is full of vitamin A.

Fish protein is especially beneficial for physical development and health. Recently, scientists' interest has focused on the study of its iodine content. Because foods rich in iodine can prevent throat diseases.

The amount of iodine contained in various types of fish varies. Crab is the least, shrimp is the most, while scallops and clams are in between. Generally, saltwater fish are richer in iodine.

The American Public Health Research Committee has studied fish in detail. Their conclusion: both fish and shellfish are good foods. First, they are nutritious and easy to digest. Oil, minerals, protein, and sometimes a large amount of vitamins—everything is available. Second, they are inexpensive and convenient for the common people.

Record of Dual Life in War and Peace (77)

— The Owner of Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter 9: A Special Train Evicts Guests, Causing False Alarms; Sitting Cold in the Yamen, Petrification Becomes a Distant Thought

An Yutian, restless in his stillness, secretly thought that he had not yet met with Ye Zuozhang. Why not go directly to the yamen to visit him? He completely forgot Liang Xiaoyun's instructions and hired a car to go by himself. Relying on the fact that Little Mao had obtained a badge for him a few days ago, he hung it on the lapel of his mandarin jacket and swaggered into the yamen, searching for the Correspondence Office. Stepping inside, he saw a large reception hall filled with people of all kinds. Some were wearing military uniforms, some were in civilian clothes, some were old, some were young, some were foreigners with yellow hair and blue eyes, and there were even monks. It was like a human exhibition hall. He found an empty chair and sat down, but for a long time, no one paid attention to him. No cup of tea or cigarette was offered. Then he saw an armed military officer with the rank of major walking out of a dark room inside, holding a large handful of business cards in his hand, flipping them over and over in his palm like shuffling poker cards. People sitting nearby took their business cards and bowed and smiled at him. He guessed that this must be the correspondence officer in charge of communication, so he took out a business card with his official title printed on it, walked over, and handed it to him, saying very humbly, "Excuse me, I'm here to see the Military Governor. Please inform him." The correspondence officer rolled his eyes, looked him and his business card all over, and hummed slightly from his seemingly cold nose, "Wait a moment," and then swaggered away. He was ordered to sit back and wait. Outside, new people continued to arrive in groups, but some were arrogant and very familiar, not asking where to sit when they entered the door, but going straight to the door of the inner room, lifting the white cloth curtain, and shouting loudly, "Chief" or "Brother." Then the correspondence officer came back in, shouting, "Please come, so-and-so, please come, so-and-so." Eight or nine out of ten were those who were very familiar with the people in the inner room, and they happily agreed, following the correspondence officer out in batches. The people sitting outside were rarely called, only watching others go in and out like a revolving lantern, and still had to sit upright and quietly, waiting for their turn. This wait lasted for more than four hours. An Yutian desperately finished a pack of cigarettes, only making his lips dry and his heart restless, his legs sore and his waist aching, and his hunger and thirst intensifying, but he could not get any accurate information about whether he would be seen or not, and he could not just leave. He couldn't help thinking to himself, "Am I going to be imprisoned again?" If I continue to sit and wait like this, it will not be difficult to turn my body into a natural fossil. When will this crime be over? Let's wait for the next chapter to explain.

Finance

Last Week's Gold Price

Rose by Nine Taels and One Qian

No significant fluctuations. Last week, the standard gold price tended to be firm again, but there were no major fluctuations. The daily fluctuations were only four or five taels, with a maximum of eight taels. There were no important overseas news. The price fell from the beginning of the week, opening at 712.5 taels. Due to the impact of the continued rise in the silver market, it eventually saw a low price of 711.8 qian. However, there was talk that the Central Bank would transport cash for export, and the price then rose. However, the US silver price reported a fall, and the exchange rate trended lower, especially with the exhaustion of cash and the Central Bank absorbing it. As a result, the market price advanced and broke through 700 taels. By Wednesday, due to the traditional Dragon Boat Festival, there was a holiday. Then, with the swap date approaching, various parties planned to push the price up significantly, estimating 10 taels. However, according to the US dollar rate, the July to August swap should be a discount of 25 (equivalent to 6 taels). This made the shorts fearful and they covered their positions, reaching a maximum of 729 taels on Friday. However, the price then reacted slightly as sellers seemed to be active. The closing price on Saturday was 724.8 taels, an increase of 9.1 qian compared to the previous Saturday. The total review of the gold week was a gain of 17.2 qian. As for the overseas silver market, the British price was flat and the US price fell. The exchange rate calculated that the British rate against the US rate fell by 1.875 points, and the US rate against the British rate rose by 0.125 points. As a result, the Shanghai HSBC listing calculated that the British gold price was flat and the US gold price decreased slightly. Internally, the British gold price was flat, and the US gold price decreased recently by 1.875, and forward by 3.125. This was really due to the exchange rate relationship. Gold firms covered their recent positions and sold their forward positions, sometimes hedging with strips. However, the settlement price was around 70 taels. According to the exchange, the total number of suspicious codes was 23,200. Various firms such as Wanxing Shunli and the Dalian gang still accounted for most of the long positions. Qian Changxiang actually had more than 5,000, and Yifeng Yong also had more than 3,000. Yuanxing Yongbing Xing and others were also the same. The Guangdong gang had only a few more. The shorts included Yuan Mao Yong, Dade Cheng, and each had more than 2,000. The rest were mostly retail customers. The following is a summary of the situation over the week.

Review of the peaceful five days (Monday): The big strip of silver continued to rise by 0.0625, the US silver price rose by 0.25, and the exchange rate was flat, so the initial US dollar listing was unchanged, and the internal price was also flat. The standard gold price initially opened down by 3.2 qian, at 712.5 taels, and then by 13.5 qian. However, there were many sellers, and the price eventually fell to 711.8 qian. Soon after, news came that the Central Bank was shipping cash out, and the market improved immediately. Buyers were aggressive, pushing the price up to 19.6 qian, but it soon retreated to 16.6 qian. Sellers were also active, and the price closed at 17.4 qian at noon. The afternoon opened at 16.7 qian, and the Guangdong gang entered, pushing the price to 18.8 qian. The price closed at 18 taels, an increase of 2.3 qian compared to the previous Saturday. The situation was complex, rising and falling, with a fluctuation of 7.8 qian throughout the day. Fuyu Hengyu Zhifeng Yong and a Mr. Wu followed the price up.

(Tuesday): The big strip was unchanged, the silver price was down, the initial listing was the same as before, and the internal British price was firm and the US price was soft, so the exchange rate was slightly lower. The gold market opened at 719.5 taels, up 1.5 taels. Then, large investors competed to buy, pushing the price above 720 taels, to 24.2 qian. The closing price was 20.8 qian. The afternoon opened at 20 taels, then at 21.6 qian. The market was quite calm, with little trading. The closing price was 20.06 qian, an increase of 2.6 qian from the previous day. The daily fluctuation was 6 taels.

(Wednesday): The big strip continued to rise by 0.0625, the silver price fell by 0.125, and the exchange rates all reported lower. However, due to the Dragon Boat Festival, the banks were closed, so the gold market was also closed for a day.

There were no new developments in domestic and international affairs. Major investors remained cautious, supply and demand were balanced, and prices did not fluctuate significantly. Furthermore, since the war, various industries in the local area have not been able to recover easily, the market is sluggish, and finances are stagnant. With the end of the previous settlement period approaching, various businesses needed to finalize their accounts. Although there were still those investing and receiving income, most adopted a cautious attitude and there were no large-scale transactions. Consequently, supply exceeded demand, and prices fluctuated and declined, but the trend remained relatively stable, with daily fluctuations of only a few cents. As a result, compared to the previous week, only the Reorganization Surtax Bond experienced a minor increase of about half a yuan, while most others fell by one to 1.67 yuan. Only the Series 20 Salt Tax Bond showed a significant decline of about one yuan for the next month's delivery. Observing the current environment, one feels a sense of stagnation. If the overall situation does not improve significantly in the short term, the future will become even more desolate, and a turnaround is unlikely. Therefore, before the end of the previous settlement period, there is little hope for development in the bond market. Panic Selling by Nervous Investors

Last Week's Yarn Market Trending Soft

Gloomy Global Trends, Few Reasons for Optimism

The long-brewing yarn market suddenly showed cracks last week, with the market trending towards softness. A decline had been possible for some time. Due to the thin local inventory and the continuous, albeit small, demand for spot yarn in the south, bulls held on tightly. However, overseas cotton yarn conditions became increasingly unstable, with American cotton breaking through the five-cent barrier. Domestically, social and economic bankruptcies and rural decline were frequently reported, raising concerns about future yarn sales. This triggered panic among investors, leading to a flood of new selling. Consequently, the market downturn intensified. Some, however, still believed the base was small and remained bullish. Yet, global prices are plummeting, making it difficult for local yarn to remain stable compared to foreign yarn. The high price of local yarn in the past was due to certain reasons. Recently, the cost of raw materials has become extremely low, reducing the cost of cotton yarn itself. Therefore, the situation is vastly different. Japanese merchants are aggressively selling yarn in all directions, reportedly at exceptionally low prices with profit margins still available. As a result, North China is flooded with their products, leaving local yarn with little hope. With the low cost of raw materials, local factories are eager to sell to compete. Some manufacturers are reportedly struggling with inventory. There are also reports that the clearance of Tianjin local yarn is sluggish, with some planning to ship it to Shanghai to find a way out. This demonstrates the immature business strategies of local factories. In conclusion, the global trends are grim, with few reasons for optimism. According to statistics, during the past week, various groups purchased a total of 3,415 bales of spot yarn, with 307 bales traded among peers. Prices were 3-4 liang lower than the previous week. Large investors were selling standard yarn, and bulls were liquidating. Prices for various months were 4 liang 7, 8, and 9 qian lower than the previous week. The total transaction volume for the week was 120,950 bales. The following is a breakdown of the amount purchased by each group:

Amidst the Global Cotton Market's Plunge

Last Week's Cotton Market Extremely Weak

The cotton market was quite unstable last week, with a sharp decline. The global cotton market was plunging, and American cotton reached a new low not seen in a century, breaking through the five-cent barrier. This triggered widespread panic. Shanghai trading houses were selling American cotton, middling grade, at 27 liang, with a rebate of one liang. The larger the quantity, the lower the price. However, factories, seeing the unfavorable trend, were unwilling to absorb it, resulting in no transactions. This cotton could be used to produce 20-count yarn. As news spread, anxiety increased in the market. Large investors were selling, causing the market to decline significantly. However, Shanghai cotton merchants generally believed that 29 liang for standard cotton was cheap, as such a price had not been seen for years, and they considered it a good buying opportunity. Therefore, they were purchasing daily. However, the low price of American cotton and global prices were unprecedented. (Eleventh, Tokyo Dispatch from Telegraph Agency) According to information obtained by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the American cotton market has been gradually declining due to favorable weather in the cotton-producing areas and political instability before the general election. The July contract has plummeted to a new low of over four cents. The authorities in Texas estimate that the carryover of old cotton on August 1st will increase by around 13 million bales. Moreover, cotton-producing countries also expect an increase in production this year, which will significantly reduce the sales of American cotton. They predict that American cotton will fall to over one cent this fall (i.e., over two fen). Predicting prices to fall below two fen seems excessively low. Overall, observing the general trend, there is little reason for optimism. Compared to the situation of foreign cotton, how can local cotton stand? It is said that there are sufficient stocks in the northern region, and a large amount has not yet been shipped out. It is difficult to predict the future of standard cotton. The price of standard cotton fell by 1 liang 89 qian in a week. The total transaction volume for the week was 200,500 dan. The amount of Yao flower cotton arriving at the docks was 2,770 bales, and Tong flower cotton was 150 bales. The following is a breakdown of the amount of spot cotton purchased by each factory:
