Silk and Tea: The Overseas Chinese Silk Market Last Week

Filled with a Chorus of Declines

Frequently Showing Unprecedented New Low Prices

During the past week, the local foreign trading houses' silk market has fallen into despair. Since the economic decline in Europe and America, silk weaving factories have heavily used rayon in order to reduce costs, leading to a significant decrease in the consumption of raw silk. Although Japanese silk merchants have lowered prices in an attempt to sell old silk, there is insufficient demand, and there is still no hope for a turnaround in silk sales. Local silk follows the downward trend of Japanese silk, and the decline has not weakened. New lows, unprecedented in history, have repeatedly appeared. Factories still experience activity without sales. Wires from Shanghai still show little turning towards Shanghai. The futures and spot silk markets continued to be quiet during the week. Manufacturers have 30,000 to 40,000 bales of old silk in their hands, but there is no way to sell them. New silks from Jiangsu and Zhejiang have already been shipped to Shanghai. Only one-tenth of the silk factories in the city have started operating, and most are reeling old cocoons for customers. New silk has not been released, and the market is stagnant. There is no hope for improvement in silk sales in the short term. Last week, overseas Chinese silk prices were filled with a chorus of declines. There were daily transactions without sales, making it scarcely worth recording.

Pongee and Oiled Cloth Raincoats Enjoy Temporary Boom

The pongee and oiled cloth market has been increasing steadily in recent years. Sales were even better during the early spring season. As the rainy season is approaching, sales are even more brisk. Each week, foreign firms are shipping around 20 pieces. However, market prices remain weak and declining. This is because there is too much supply. Oiled cloth raincoats are currently the most popular item. As a result, sales have been particularly widespread. They are very popular in Shanghai, and most Western-style raincoats are made from this material. Yesterday, wholesale prices for local goods were 1 yuan, 2 liang, and 7 qian 5 fen per yard. (Last year, when it first arrived in Shanghai, it was sold for 3 liang 8 and 9 qian). Purple-brown and brown are more popular than gray. All the large and small Western clothing stores in the local area have purchased them.

Seaweed and Shrimp: Thriving Sales of Fresh Yangsheng

First Harvest of 8,000 Dan... Market Prices Decline

The new spring seaweed and shrimp have been thriving. Fishing boats setting sail from places such as Qushan, Daishan, Zhoushan, and Luohua in Ningbo are returning fully loaded. It is estimated that the total amount collected from various mountains has reached 8,000 dan. Moreover, there is still a second harvest to be had. If the weather is sunny and the fish schools do not disperse, it would not be surprising to collect another 3,000 to 4,000 dan. Such abundance is rare. Last year's total was only 5,600 to 5,700 dan, so this year's amount is more than double. Therefore, fishermen are beaming with joy. However, with so much supply, prices are declining. Yesterday, top-grade goods were sold at 28 liang, and ordinary goods were sold at 27 liang to 26 liang. Buyers from other regions were unenthusiastic, and local traders were unwilling to hold large inventories. Therefore, prices may continue to weaken.

Say

Special Tribunal for Punishing Corruption

— Buddha

A dispatch from Beijing the day before yesterday stated that the Ministry of Justice is drafting regulations for punishing corruption and organizational rules for the special tribunal. Once the draft is completed, it will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for approval and promulgation.

Under this honest and clean government, there should no longer be corrupt officials who embezzle and pervert the law. However, in recent years, looking at the various ministries and agencies, there is no evidence of virtuous governance. Instead, we hear that someone bought a large Western-style house as a residence, someone else bought a large garden as a villa, someone recently married a beautiful wife, and someone else took in a seductive concubine. I cannot understand where such vast sums of money come from to support their extravagant and luxurious lives under this clean government. This is a significant point of suspicion.

"Punishing those who steal hooks but making lords of those who steal countries" has been the traditional policy in Chinese politics. Now, with the establishment of a special court to punish corruption, it is naturally a misfortune for a few hook-stealing fellows. However, hook-stealers are everywhere, and punishing them is endless and futile. In the end, it will only be another pro forma article, "Killing a chicken to scare the monkeys." Otherwise, they will be placed in a position beyond the law, and the so-called "swans fly into the dark, how can the archer catch them?"

Therefore, it is said that the law cannot be enforced if those above violate it.

Literature

Impromptu Poem on Hearing of Commander-in-Chief Chiang's Visit to Mount Luofu

— Chen Tianmin

Your military might shakes the nine provinces,

To serve the country, what more could one seek?

Since Yue Fei, loyal and true,

You are the foremost general, unique.

You gracefully retreat to Luofu's peak,

Resembling Qi Wang's lakeside quest.

With the nation unsettled, you yearn to hide,

Deep sorrow in your heart, sorely pressed.

Your moral integrity, a century submerged,

Who will raise hearts from the depths of disgrace?

You alone uphold virtue's banner high,

In wind and rain, like a rooster crowing, admired by all.

Science

Talking About Wireless

— Ding Zhuzhong

"Wireless" is the abbreviation for "wireless telegraph," "wireless telephone," and "wireless imaging." To understand the advantages of "wireless," one must first understand the disadvantages of "wired telegraph" and "wired telephone":

(1) When the distance between two places is too great, the cost of wires and poles is too high. Submarine cables between East Asia and Europe and America cost millions of dollars per line.

(2) Inspecting wires and poles is extremely inconvenient, especially for submarine cables. A submarine cable across the Atlantic Ocean was laid between Ireland and Newfoundland in 1865, but it broke and was lost before it could be completed. It took many years to find it.

(3) Aircraft in the air and ships at sea cannot be equipped with fixed wires, so they cannot communicate with various places, especially in times of danger, when it is simply impossible to call for help.

(4) The inhumane wars in the world often aim to cut off the enemy's wires. All other undertakings are bound to be greatly affected.

(5) The length of the wire and the size of the electrical energy are inversely proportional. The longer the wire, the smaller the electrical energy. Therefore, telephones cannot reach when the distance between two places is too great.

In order to eliminate these shortcomings and contribute the most economical and effective products to mankind, scientists have continued to work hard to improve them. Sure enough, on December 12, 1901, science released a surprising light: Marconi received a telegram from the United States in England. This telegram, which crossed the Atlantic Ocean, was not transmitted using wires. There were no overhead wires on land, and no submarine cables in the water.

Marconi was an Italian, and he could not get experimental funding in his own country, so he went to England. In 1894, he received funding from the British Telegraph Bureau and began experimenting with "wireless telegraph." In 1896, he successfully experimented, but could only communicate over a distance of 1 and 3/4 miles (about 5 li). By 189, British warships could communicate over a distance of 85 miles (about 240 li). Later, he worked hard to improve the communication distance gradually increased, eventually enabling "wireless telegraph" to reach the globe.

He further sought improvement in "wireless telegraph" and successfully experimented with "wireless telephone" in 1908. Since 1918, due to the invention of the vacuum tube (i.e., the light bulb on the wireless radio), "wireless"

progressed rapidly. Therefore, "wireless telephone" can broadcast beautiful music or speeches by famous people to the world, so that people around the world can listen through radios, as if they were gathered in the same room.

The American Telephone and Telegraph Company and the Western Electric Company worked together to invent "telephotography" and successfully experimented with it in 1925. This involves using changes in electric current to transmit images of people or other objects or calligraphy from one place to another. For example, in May 1926, Americans transmitted photos from Ohio to New York. However, the transmission between the two places was done using wires. In July 1927, the French invented "wireless telephotography," which, like wireless telegraph and telephone, eliminated the wires used to transmit electricity between the two places. Modern scientists are competing to research and develop, with very significant results.

Looking at it this way, all the sounds and images in the world cannot be blocked by mountains and rivers after all. The ancient sayings "thousand-mile eyes, smooth-sailing ears" have now been confirmed by science.

Learning to Write and Sketch

Such a School

— Iwano

Old Wang had been eating the rice of the south for more than ten years, but he was still so poor that his family was destitute. He thought that if things continued like this, he wouldn't be able to support his family, let alone himself. He saw that the sound of chanting and singing was endless in the alleys and neighborhoods of Shanghai, and he thought that opening a school would be a good business. Once he made up his mind, he figured out a way to raise 200 gold coins, rented a single building in a small alley, and lived with his wife and children in a pavilion upstairs. The upstairs was rented out to others, and the downstairs living room was used as a classroom. He got more than a dozen desks and chairs, a blackboard, bought a bell, and bought a few paper national flags to hang in the air. It looked very much like a school. The lead school sign had already been hung at the door, and recruitment advertisements had also been posted. Children with snotty noses from various neighborhoods came in droves, and the classroom was full. Old Wang naturally smiled when he saw this.

From then on, Old Wang began to play his role as the Monkey King and sing his solo performance. The big dog barks, the little dog jumps, and he taught them in a clear and loud voice. After teaching for a few days, he felt that it was inconvenient for one class to be taught while the others did nothing and disturbed the classroom. So he came up with a brilliant idea, which was to drive all the people who were not being taught to play in the five-foot-square patio. The whole school was divided into three classes. The first half of the day was three lessons, and it just so happened that each class had one lesson. Chen Ping cut meat, and nothing could be more even than that. The second half of the day was the same. After a week, he felt that this method was not good, because the noise from the patio would often enter through the windows, making the people in the classroom uneasy. He then pondered a way to improve it, and as a result, he came up with another brilliant idea, which was to have everyone come in and sit down. Those who were being taught listened to the teacher, and those who were not being taught wrote. From then on, it was indeed much quieter. He was very satisfied with this teaching method, and he often boasted to others about it.

Two weeks later, a bare-footed child with snot running down his face said to him, "Teacher! My dad told me to ask you, why do other schools teach arithmetic, but we don't have it here?"

This reminded Old Wang. That's right, new-style reading cannot be without arithmetic, but I haven't learned it, so how can I teach it? He thought for a long time, and then replied to the child with a stern voice, "Who said we don't have it? We'll teach it in a few days!" That night, he went to buy an arithmetic book for the first grade of elementary school, studied it hard, and after five nights of hard work, he was able to write the formula one plus one equals two, and five minus three equals two. Once he fully understood these, he immediately passed them on to the students. All three classes of students were taught addition and subtraction. The students who had already learned it were given a few more questions on the blackboard to do, saying that elementary school just needed to know addition and subtraction. As long as they did it a lot, did it quickly, and were familiar with it, they would benefit from it for the rest of their lives.

A month later, he was asked by the students to teach singing. He thought that singing was also indispensable in new-style reading, and he also thought that learning to box at the age of sixty, this "獨來米沙" could not be learned for a while. Fortunately, he had a sixteen- or seventeen-year-old nephew who was studying in the fourth grade of elementary school, so he pulled him in to teach for two hours a week. From then on, in his school, there was Chinese, there was writing, there was singing, and there was addition and subtraction. He felt even more that he was a new-style school.

His school has been open for almost a year now, and he still adheres to this teaching method. I am also paying attention to whether there will be any better methods in the future. If there are any new discoveries, I will not hesitate to use my ink and pen, and I will not hesitate to use the space of this magazine to inform readers, so that those who revise the history of education in Shanghai can also get more information.

A Complaint Uttered from a Pigeon Cage

— Manqian

Since the invasion of Shanghai by the brutal Japanese, and the subsequent destruction of schools, after relocating to Shanghai to resume classes, our dormitory is a two-story Western-style building rented for us by the school. Counting the small rooms, living rooms, and side rooms, there are less than five rooms in total. Furthermore, the living room has been converted into a dining hall. Naturally, seventy or eighty people live here, crammed together like sardines in a can.

In the past, when the weather was cooler, being crowded was bearable, but now the weather is getting hotter every day. A dozen or twenty people crammed together emanate waves of sweaty odor, penetrating directly into our nostrils. In addition, we all sleep on the floor, rendering mosquito nets ineffective. Consequently, mosquitoes and gnats reign supreme at night, preventing a good night's sleep. Therefore, classrooms, balconies, and rooftops have gradually become our colonies. Although it is troublesome to roll up our bedding early and spread it out late, it is much better than being crammed together.

As for the classrooms, they are in rented houses nearby. The classrooms are only half the size of normal ones. Shanghai's air is already polluted, and with thirty or forty people breathing in one room, the discomfort inside is unimaginable. Sometimes it is so stifling that almost the entire class is yawning and wanting to sleep. Moreover, the incessant hawking of vendors outside the door makes it impossible to concentrate on our books.

Furthermore, the most difficult problem to solve is that of excretion. Originally, the house had two flushing toilets, but for some reason, one is broken. Therefore, the remaining one has to serve seventy or eighty people, which is clearly insufficient. If one suddenly needs to defecate urgently or has diarrhea, there is truly no solution.

The various situations are too numerous to fully describe. In short, under this kind of living condition, everything gives us a great sense of unease. Ah, tracing it to its root, this gift from the brutal Japanese is truly unforgettable.

Editor's Note: If the facts in this article are indeed true, we implore the landlords of the school to show some conscience and not treat the students like pigs.
